<div id="review_2048677863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2048677863" />
    <a title="Celise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4653644-celise"><img alt="Celise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546382482p2/4653644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2048677863?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celise" href="/user/show/4653644-celise">Celise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552167505" href="/book/show/15849484-witches-abroad">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=fantasy-adult">fantasy-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2048677863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16504848055604173317"><i>
  <b>"It's not staying in the same place that's the problem," said Nanny. "It's not letting your mind wander." </b>
</i><br/><br/>Witches Abroad is one of the most entertaining Discworld novels so far, if reading chronologically, in which Granny Weatherwax, Nanny Ogg, and Magrat set off on an adventure to stop a peasant girl, Emberella, from marrying a prince. Along the way the witches encounter many stories, including one with a girl in a red riding hood and a rather confused big bad wolf. Not to worry though, the</span>
  <span id="freeText16504848055604173317" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"It's not staying in the same place that's the problem," said Nanny. "It's not letting your mind wander." </b>
</i><br /><br />Witches Abroad is one of the most entertaining Discworld novels so far, if reading chronologically, in which Granny Weatherwax, Nanny Ogg, and Magrat set off on an adventure to stop a peasant girl, Emberella, from marrying a prince. Along the way the witches encounter many stories, including one with a girl in a red riding hood and a rather confused big bad wolf. Not to worry though, the three witches have many talents in derailing things that are meant to be.<br /><br />As usual, one's enjoyment of a Discworld novel is usually determined foremost by the cast of characters, and secondly by where on the scale of ridiculous the concept falls. Somewhere in the middle is usually good, and this one is just that. The three witches are such a perfect ensemble that the comedy comes through really well, and the story seems to unfold naturally around them. Sure, it's still ridiculous, but the parody of classic princess stories is easy to make sense of. Accompanied by Greebo, Nanny's vile cat Greebo (who could stop a stampede of bulls in its tracks with one glare), Death himself, and several recognizable storybook characters, this is will probably be one of the more memorable books once I've gotten through all 40.<br /><br />Just as an extra note- I always get a kick out of how Death's never mentioned by name in most of the books besides his intro in Colour of Magic and in his own series, and is only indicated by the all-caps manner of speaking. I had a few laughs over that in this one, as small as his part might have been. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16504848055604173317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3350520338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3350520338" />
    <a title="Dylan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/91403015-dylan"><img alt="Dylan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593901230p2/91403015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3350520338?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dylan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dylan" href="/user/show/91403015-dylan">Dylan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062237361" href="/book/show/16248255-witches-abroad">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/91403015-dylan?shelf=discworld">discworld</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/91403015-dylan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3350520338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11232224090353790627"><b>"Humanity is a nice place to visit, but you wouldn't want to stay."</b><br/><br/>Terry Pratchett's 12th installment of Discworld sees our three favorite witches on a whistle-stop tour of fairy tales on their way to stop a girl from marrying a prince. Lots of pumpkins are involved. There's also gumbo.<br/><br/>This is another great entry into the series, certainly one of the strongest, drawing on fairy tales and a few other things that should be fairly familiar to most people, but Pratchett puts his own spin on it and h</span>
  <span id="freeText11232224090353790627" style="display:none"><b>"Humanity is a nice place to visit, but you wouldn't want to stay."</b><br /><br />Terry Pratchett's 12th installment of Discworld sees our three favorite witches on a whistle-stop tour of fairy tales on their way to stop a girl from marrying a prince. Lots of pumpkins are involved. There's also gumbo.<br /><br />This is another great entry into the series, certainly one of the strongest, drawing on fairy tales and a few other things that should be fairly familiar to most people, but Pratchett puts his own spin on it and hilarity ensues. This was definitely one of the more "laugh-out-loud" Discworlds for me so far. <br /><br />Esme, Gytha and Magrat are all in fine form and it was nice to see them a little bit out of their comfort zone in this one. The supporting characters aren't quite as strong in this one I feel, but the three witches (and particularly Esme and Gytha in this one) are strong enough for that to not really matter. <br /><br />The plot is a fun one, I felt that it was maybe a tad weaker than some of the other Discworlds but this was more than made up for by Pratchett's inclusion and spin on so many classic fairytales and such.<br /><br />The only disappointment that I had was that there weren't as many footnotes as there usually are, and those are often the best bits. Still though, another fantastic Discworld book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11232224090353790627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1987800597" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987800597" />
    <a title="Wol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5973651-wol"><img alt="Wol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518815855p2/5973651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1987800597?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wol" href="/user/show/5973651-wol">Wol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973651-wol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5973651-wol?shelf=r-fantasy-bingo-2017">r-fantasy-bingo-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1987800597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer719787714036147491">The first of the Discworld novels I have read (publication order, mostly, but I skipped Reaper Man and will be going back to that one next) that I have finished and immediately thought: "Everything about that was absolutely perfect". <br/><br/>The easy chemistry between Nanny and Granny is not only hilarious but unerringly truthful in a way that most fictional friendships aren't. How often do Nanny and Granny think something negative about one another but wisely keep their mouths shut about it in the mome</span>
  <span id="freeText719787714036147491" style="display:none">The first of the Discworld novels I have read (publication order, mostly, but I skipped Reaper Man and will be going back to that one next) that I have finished and immediately thought: "Everything about that was absolutely perfect". <br /><br />The easy chemistry between Nanny and Granny is not only hilarious but unerringly truthful in a way that most fictional friendships aren't. How often do Nanny and Granny think something negative about one another but wisely keep their mouths shut about it in the moment? This is because they know one another inside out, they know that it would lead to nothing good, they accept one another's shortcomings and in real friendships <i>this is a thing that we do all the time</i>. I love them. <br /><br />That's not to say that Magrat doesn't have her place in the trio, and in Witches Abroad she certainly did her best to be more assertive, but ultimately her ongoing identity crisis continues to be her defining feature. And that's kind of the point, so it's OK.<br /><br />The absolute highlight of the novel for me was the "Northern English biddies on holiday" aspect of it. I couldn't help it. I'm from Lancashire myself (which Lancre is based on) and Granny in particular is a spot on take on the Northern tourist of the 80s who thinks garlic bread is an exotic delicacy and anything more daring can safely be filed under "foreign muck". Nanny is so much like my own dear departed Grandmother that at times I was laughing and misty eyed at the same time. <br /><br />The twisted take on fairytales and how we're shaped by stories was brilliantly executed, and at times even pretty disturbing for Discworld (the part with the wolf actually made my skin a bit prickly). The underlying social commentary is very Pratchett: Forcing people into what you have deemed to be the "correct" narrative is wrong. Leave others be to live their lives. It was relevant then, it's relevant now and no doubt it will continue to be so. <br /><br />Brilliant stuff. This is certainly going to be a comfort read for me in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="719787714036147491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1754511050" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1754511050" />
    <a title="Marina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2938801-marina"><img alt="Marina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446555789p2/2938801.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1754511050?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marina" href="/user/show/2938801-marina">Marina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473200265" href="/book/show/20494122-witches-abroad">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2938801-marina?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2938801-marina?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1754511050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7163976672113376802">I'm getting used to the fact that the Witches Collection is not a consecutive story like The City Watch was, at least not really. There isn't really one overarching theme, except to play around with story tropes, shake them up, traumatize and scare them, make fun of them when they cry and then send them back home with a lolly-pop. <br/><br/>The Witches series is hilarious. I love these characters and how much we're getting to know them and how comical and even slightly idiotic they seem, yet how poignant </span>
  <span id="freeText7163976672113376802" style="display:none">I'm getting used to the fact that the Witches Collection is not a consecutive story like The City Watch was, at least not really. There isn't really one overarching theme, except to play around with story tropes, shake them up, traumatize and scare them, make fun of them when they cry and then send them back home with a lolly-pop. <br /><br />The Witches series is hilarious. I love these characters and how much we're getting to know them and how comical and even slightly idiotic they seem, yet how poignant they are once you stop and think about it. The big question in Witches Abroad is what happens when you try to force a story? What happens when you take well known and beloved tropes and characters and force them to act out the same story again and again, even it no longer works anyone? The answer is something closer to what Stephen King writes than the Grim brothers. It's morphs into a horror story in which unwilling people are forced to do things they are not meant to otherwise. What if Cinderella didn't want to go to the ball? Or get married? What if she liked being a servant? Who's the fairy godmother to make her? You can't save someone who doesn't need to be saved.<br /><br />Either way, great installment of the Witches series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7163976672113376802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('58oyeNpanr0ghs66JqbPKJogyRK37x/scudEppurhKjd7FuqYQRX1YetetvRU8X3TH8u2nlikYspmQIXVuh2Mg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iVrf1tZdlZtekeCu42WU8njTCekf1Ts4ZyfAhMqyI3+zfLYEbQNc8/m6VM8UkJ4trozuIdFYtV88WYY1B/HR5Q==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3818711477991293428">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText3818711477991293428" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3818711477991293428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
